After the Sale of the China and Foreign Telephone Company, the Ministry of Communications is Preparing to Recover It

Prepare cash at the actual price to recover the Chinese shares; After the sale of the Shanghai China and Foreign Telephone Company, the Ministry of Communications is still proceeding with the method of recovering sovereignty. Yesterday, the Municipal Chamber of Commerce also received a letter from the Ministry notifying all Chinese shareholders not to transfer their equity to foreigners. The Ministry can prepare cash at the actual price to recover it. The original letter and notice are recorded below:

Original Letter from the Ministry of Communications; Sirs, Regarding the case of the Shanghai China and Foreign Telephone Company being sold to the International Telephone and Telegraph Corporation in June of the 19th year and renamed the Shanghai Telephone Company, and the Shanghai Concession authorities arbitrarily approving the 40-year telephone franchise, it not only infringes upon our national sovereignty but also hinders the progress of recovering the Concession. When the Ministry heard of this proposal beforehand, it prepared to negotiate in September of the 18th year and advocated that the government prepare the price to recover it. On one hand, the Ministry requested the Ministry of Foreign Affairs to instruct the Shanghai Jiangsu Negotiator and the Shanghai Office to seriously negotiate with the Shanghai Consul Corps. On the other hand, it prepared to implement the procedures for recovery. However, the Shanghai Consul Corps and the Public Works Department authorities had no sincerity and deliberately delayed the protests and negotiations of our government. They also allowed the China and Foreign Company to proceed with the sale. On June 12 of the 19th year, the Ministry of Foreign Affairs approved the Ministry's request and issued a declaration in Chinese and English, stating that the Chinese government could not recognize any method of the China and Foreign Telephone Company's sale to foreign merchants, in preparation for future negotiations. At the same time, the Ministry also requested the Shanghai business community and the Chinese directors of the Concession to provide assistance. At that time, the public sent many letters and telegrams and were able to cooperate quite well. However, the company's board of directors attributed all measures to the shareholders, and the Chinese shareholders were mostly scattered small shareholders and lacked unity. As a result, although the Chinese shareholders were absent and protested against the company's bidding method, it was easily passed by the Western shareholders in the company. Negotiations have not been successful for more than a year, which is regrettable. However, the Ministry's determination to recover the Shanghai Concession telephone has not changed because of this. Now that the company has disregarded the protests of our government and people and has brazenly implemented the transfer, our government can only use effective methods to remedy the situation. The Ministry has repeatedly consulted with the Ministry of Foreign Affairs and decided to proceed from the practical side to gradually recover the sovereignty. The State Council has approved the proposal and is now implementing it step by step. However, this matter is of great importance, and its success still depends on the efforts of the public, and the unity of the Chinese shareholders is particularly important. It is found that the original shareholders of the company, the Chinese shareholders, actually accounted for 47%. If they could have united and cooperated to protest at that time, the company's sale plan could have been cancelled. In view of this past, it is even more necessary to make plans early to seek unity. It is known that your association is a gathering place for Chinese merchants and has a long-standing reputation. I hope that you will take the lead in leading and supporting the government. I am now enclosing a detailed list of the names and addresses of the Chinese shareholders of the Shanghai Telephone Company and ask you to notify the Chinese shareholders to register with your association and not to sell the shares to foreigners again. If you want to sell, the Ministry will prepare cash at the actual price to recover them. This method will enable a complete statistical count of the Chinese shares and will not be difficult to gradually recover the Shanghai Concession telephone. I am corresponding to you accordingly, hoping that you will investigate and reply with the progress of the handling. Sincerely, Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce.

Notice from the Municipal Chamber of Commerce; The case of the Shanghai China and Foreign Telephone Company being sold to the International Telephone Company and renamed the Shanghai Telephone Company was decided after consultation with the Ministry of Foreign Affairs to gradually recover the sovereignty from the practical side, and the State Council approved it. It is now being implemented step by step. The original shareholders of the company, the Chinese shares, actually accounted for 47%. The unity of the shareholders is particularly important. The names of the Chinese shareholders of the Shanghai Telephone Company are now enclosed. Please notify the Chinese shareholders to register with the Chamber of Commerce and not to sell the shares to foreigners again. If you want to sell, the Ministry will prepare cash at the actual price to recover them, etc. The matter is related to protecting sovereignty, and the government has already decided on a method of gradual recovery. All nationals should sincerely support it. Moreover, the Ministry of Communications has promised to prepare cash at the actual price to recover them, and there is no damage to the actual interests of the Chinese shares. It is the same sale, and it should be allowed to be taken over by the Ministry of Communications in order to prevent the gradual recovery plan from being interrupted. I am afraid that the addresses of the shareholders have changed and the letters may be incorrect. A special announcement is hereby published in the newspaper instead of sending individual letters. I hope you will appreciate it.

Sinking of the Changjiang

Three female passengers and eleven crew members drowned; Sixty-two crew members and passengers rescued arrived in Shanghai yesterday; Total loss of ship and cargo estimated at over 1 million; The Shanghai Shipping Company's Changjiang liner, managed by Kang Zhenji of Renji Road in this city, was returning to Shanghai from Annan Haiphong when it met with an accident at the junction of the Fuzhou and Wenzhou sea areas. Fourteen people died, including passengers, crew members, and stokers. Sixty-two crew members were rescued and returned to Shanghai yesterday by a French warship. Our reporter went to various parties to record the details of the ship's accident as follows:

Reef Trapped Under Hull; The Changjiang liner, flying the French flag and traveling between Shanghai and Vietnam, was carrying coal back to Shanghai from Haiphong on the 13th. It was originally scheduled to enter the port on the morning of the 18th, but at 2:00 PM on the 16th, when it was sailing to the junction of the Min and Ou sea areas in the North Yushan sea area, a thick fog occurred. At that time, it was heard that the first mate was on duty and the shipowner, Krathat, was resting in the room. The ship suddenly struck a reef outside North Yushan in the fog. The bottom of its second hold was immediately trapped by the reef and the hull was broken, allowing seawater to enter the ship. However, it was not immediately submerged.

Reversing Engine Breaks Bottom, Sinks Ship; Upon receiving the report, the shipowner hurried out of the cabin to observe, thinking that he could find a way to escape the danger. He immediately ordered the driver, Goodmus, to quickly reverse the engine so that it could retreat back into the sea. The driver and stoker dared not disobey and immediately reversed the engine. Unexpectedly, the reef trapped in the second hold was very sharp. As soon as the engine was reversed, the hull retreated, but the bottom of the second hold had been split into two, and a large amount of seawater entered the hull, causing it to sink immediately. Most of the crew members and passengers on board were unable to escape and drowned.

Fourteen Lives Lost; Hull Split Open, Ship Sinks Immediately; In total, it only took ten minutes from hitting the reef to sinking. At this time, the crew members, stokers, sailors, servants, and passengers on board rushed to the deck to untie the lifeboats in an attempt to escape. There were eight passengers in the cabin who came to Shanghai from Hong Kong, including five men and three women. After the three female passengers grabbed a lifeboat on the deck, they untied the rope and lowered it into the sea. Unexpectedly, one end of the hanging rope was not untied in a hurry and the lifeboat was lowered, causing it to capsize. The three female passengers (all Cantonese) fell into the sea and were immediately swept away by the huge waves. The bodies of the deceased have not been found. The other 73 crew members and male passengers competed for eight lifeboats and hurriedly lowered them into the sea. Unexpectedly, the ship sank too quickly and the ropes could not be untied. All eight lifeboats also capsized into the sea. Of these 73 people, two servants, four stokers, one foreign kitchen chief steward, one person from the management department, and three cooks, totaling eleven people, all drowned because they did not know how to swim.

Passengers Climb Mountain to Hide; After the lifeboats capsized, more than fifty crew members, sailors, stokers, and passengers swam and climbed up a small island opposite North Yushan to temporarily hide because the small island was only twenty-odd feet away from the shipwreck. These fifty-odd people stayed on the island for one night and a half a day. The clothes on each person's body were completely wet and there were no changes, and there was no food and they were hungry and cold for twenty hours. At 9:00 AM on the 17th, the villagers of North Yushan opposite saw the crew members living on the small island and sent eight small sampans to rescue the fifty-odd people, giving them food and clothing to change into while waiting for rescue.

Shipowner Sends for Help; When the ship was in distress, the shipowner sent a radio distress signal, which was first received by an American ship. Because it could not be found at that time, it was sent to Shanghai on its behalf. Kang Zhenji of the Shanghai Company received the report and immediately sent a radio message to Fujian to inquire, but no one accepted it. Kang Zhenji also went to the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company to ask them to send a telegram to the Wenzhou branch to inquire on their behalf. The Wenzhou branch ordered Haiyan to inquire, but the ship had already sunk, so they telegraphed back to Shanghai saying that it could not be found. Therefore, there was a rumor for a time that the Changjiang was missing.

Japanese Ship Relays Telegram, French Warship Arrives; The day after the ship's accident, the crew members and others had been rescued to North Yushan. The shipowner also left the ship to the mountain and hung a distress flag on the North Yushan lighthouse. At that time, a Japanese ship passed by and saw the distress signal and relayed a telegram to the French warship in Zhoushan, informing them of the location of the ship's accident. The French warship Mengna then sailed to the rescue.

Number of People Rescued; The French warship Mengna arrived off North Yushan at 10:00 AM on the 18th. At that time, it wanted to rescue the people on the mountain back to Shanghai, but the waves were extremely large and the sampan was overturned as soon as it was put into the sea. The French warship had to anchor at sea and wait for the waves to subside before rescuing them again. It was not until about 8:00 AM on the 19th that the waves subsided. The French warship then put the sampan into the sea and sailed to North Yushan, rescuing the shipowner, the first and second mates, and 57 other crew members, as well as five passengers, and sailed back to Shanghai. At about 1:00 PM, the ship arrived in Shanghai and anchored off the Jingjiang River in the outer ocean. The Jiangnan small barge was dispatched to carry the rescued people ashore.

Currently Temporarily Residing in French Concession Police Station; The 62 crew members and passengers who were rescued were first led by Kang Zhenji to Tailai Inn for lunch, and then sent to the French Concession Police Station. The police station specially set aside a room in the Songshan Road Police Station for the people to live in. When the reporter arrived at the police station, he saw that the rescued people were all in ragged clothes and were very embarrassed. Among the crew members and workers, there were many Cantonese and Ningbo people, and there were also Annamese people. They are waiting for the company to send them back to their hometowns.

Company's Post-Accident Arrangements; Kang Zhenji has not yet expressed any post-accident arrangements for the victims, and the shipowner's accident report has not yet been submitted. It is heard that the company is currently planning to buy ship tickets for the crew members in the police station and send them back to Annan, Guangdong, and Ningbo, and plans to pay them wages. Another plan to provide compensation for the deceased stokers, servants, cooks, etc. is under discussion.

Huge Sum of Money Also Sinks; The cargo carried by the ship from Annan to Shanghai was coal. After arriving in Hong Kong, more than 30 boxes of silver dollars were added, totaling 160,000 to 170,000 yuan. There were also 1,000-odd new purple copper bars, which were also very expensive. They all sank together. The loss of only part of the cargo in the ship is at least 400,000 to 500,000 yuan. The personal clothes and luggage of the crew members and workers were also completely lost.

Total Ship Loss; The ship weighed 4,500 tons and was built in 1907. The hull was still in good condition. According to the company, the loss of the ship's hull would be more than 500,000 yuan.

Page 14

Including cargo and cash, the estimated loss is more than one million. When the French warship left North Yushan yesterday, the chimney of the Changjiang had also sunk, leaving only about two feet of the mast wood top on the sea surface. The bottom of the ship was split open and there was no hope of salvaging it.

Another Report of the French Warship's Righteous Deed; It is also reported that at 3:00 PM on the 17th of this month, the radio in the French Concession of this city suddenly received a distress signal from the Changjiang on North Yushan, saying that it had hit a reef and needed help. It immediately notified the French warship Namaer, which was berthed in the Huangpu River, to rush to the rescue. It has now returned to Shanghai yesterday. A total of five passengers and sixty-five crew members were rescued in this operation and brought to Shanghai. The Chief of Police of the French Concession has sent personnel to take care of them and provide the victims with clothing, food, and other items. The injured will be sent to the hospital for treatment, and they will be sent back to their hometowns when a convenient ship passes through Shanghai.

Transfer of Ownership of Sanxin Yarn Factory

Workers Insist on Settling Affairs First - Labor-Management Negotiations Failed Yesterday - Day and Night Shifts Completely Stopped Yesterday

Since the announcement of the sale of the Sanxin Textile Factory on Yangshupu Road, it has attracted attention from all walks of life. The Municipal Social Bureau sent personnel to thoroughly investigate. Rong Zongjing's attempt to take over the factory the day before yesterday failed due to worker rejection. That evening, the night shift was declared closed. Yesterday afternoon at 5 p.m., representatives of labor and management negotiated a solution at the Sanxin Yarn Factory office at No. 7 Huangpu Bund Road, but no agreement was reached. The details of yesterday's situation are recorded as follows:

Yesterday's Situation

Yesterday, the Yangshupu Police Station dispatched more than 20 armed Chinese and foreign detectives to maintain order inside and outside the factory, and cavalry patrolled. In the morning, male and female day shift workers came one after another, preparing to enter the factory to work, unaware that the factory had declared a shutdown the night before, so many waited on the road. Currently, each department inside the factory is guarded by more than ten workers dispatched by the workers' relief group to prevent accidents, and notices are posted to instruct workers to strictly observe order, so the order inside the factory is very good. Male and female workers, especially male and female child laborers, waited persistently and refused to leave at the factory gate. Yesterday afternoon, the police station sent an additional 16 patrol officers to the factory for protection.

Workers' Meeting

Yesterday morning at 10 a.m., the relief group organized by the workers convened a temporary emergency meeting, attended by all staff members, union representatives, and department heads, totaling more than 200 people. It was resolved to (1) nominate Sun He, Chen Youqing, Jin Fuchu, Zhu Sanshan, Yang Desheng, Xu Zhixuan, Yu Zhisheng, and Gu Xiuyun as eight representatives responsible for negotiations; (2) demand that the factory owner compensate the workers for previously owed bonuses; (3) maintain workers' livelihoods; (4) issue workers severance pay; and (5) request lawyers Wu and Cai for legal assistance. The meeting adjourned at 12 p.m.

Workers' Petition

Yesterday afternoon, the Cotton Textile Industry Union of the Third Special District sent representatives Hou Jiahai and Gu Lansheng, among others, to submit a petition to the Municipal Social Bureau, requesting a fair mediation based on the city's labor regulations and urging prompt withdrawal of armed detectives from the factory. It is reported that after receiving the workers' request for assistance, the Social Bureau sent personnel to investigate all parties and has now completed the investigation and is properly reviewing the matter.

Negotiations Fail

Yesterday afternoon at 4 p.m., representatives of labor and management negotiated a solution at the Sanxin Yarn Factory office at No. 7 Huangpu Bund Road. Labor representatives Sun He, Chen Youqing, and others attended. Factory owner Sheng Ze Cheng's representative only allowed four labor representatives due to the number of labor representatives. The labor side refused to compromise. Sheng Ze Cheng's representative insisted, and the negotiations failed, so each representative thought that the capital side had no sincerity to accept the consultation, and they hated it very much, so they returned to the factory to report to all workers and then planned further actions.

Internal Organization

The shareholders of Sanxin Yarn Factory are Sheng Ze Cheng with six shares, Sheng Ping Cheng with two shares, and the remaining two shares belonging to Sheng's residence. The chairman of each room is Sheng Ze Cheng, the foreign manager is Yu Cihua, the manager is Sheng Yu. The factory site occupies approximately 270 acres with a capital of 4.5 million. There are a total of 70,000 spindles and more than 1,000 looms, producing 18,013 packages of yarn and 253.728 bolts of cloth per day. Yarn trademarks are Blue Dragon, Red Dragon, Golden Double Horse, etc. Cloth trademarks are Double Horse, Four Horse, Grass Cow, Rain Dog, Human Tower, Wealth, etc. There are a total of 96 staff members and more than 4,000 workers. The actual price of the sale by HSBC is reportedly 4.5 million, but the total amount of the sale by Sassoon & Co. was 5.8 million.

Two Notices

(1) Sanxin Yarn Factory posted a notice at the factory gate yesterday, stating that the factory is scheduled to temporarily close for a few days from March 20th. This notice is hereby issued. (2) The relief group organized by all staff members issued a notice yesterday, stating: Colleagues, please be aware that during this period, you should strictly observe order and refrain from any inappropriate actions. No one is allowed to leave the factory without permission. If there is an important matter, it must be reported and approved before leaving.

Soviet Russia Competes in the World Oil Market

Soviet Russia Establishes Agency in Shanghai

Recently, the Soviet Russian Oil Trust, in order to compete in the world oil market, has dispatched Mr. Li Pengnuofu as its representative to establish an office in Shanghai to contact Chinese merchants to promote Russian oil. Mr. Li told reporters yesterday that Soviet Russia now has the world's richest oil fields with 4.67 million tons of oil reserves, recently ranking third among the world's oil producing countries. However, after the successful industrialization that is now underway, it can jump to second place. Currently, Soviet Russia produces 20 million tons of oil annually, a sharp increase of more than double compared to before the war, when Soviet Russia produced only 9 million tons annually. It is estimated that in five years (i.e., by 1933), it can increase to 46 million tons, a double increase compared to the original Soviet Russian Five-Year Plan. Other oil-producing countries, due to the world's economic downturn and limited consumption, have seen a daily reduction in production. The development of Soviet Russia's oil production is partly due to its huge investment in the oil industry. The investment from October 1929 to October 1930 was 350 million rubles (accounting for about 10% of the total basic industry in the same year). In the future, more investment is needed and the quality of oil needs to be improved. Currently, gasoline factories are gradually established based on the latest American style, and their products are for domestic and export use. Exports from 1929 to 1930 were 4.62 million tons, five times higher than before the war (Russian oil exports in 1913 were 947,000 tons), and also increased by 28% compared to 1928-1929 (Russian oil exports in 1928-1929 were 3.63 million tons). Domestic consumption is also increasing daily, from 7.7455 tons in 1928-1929 to 10,115 tons in 1929-1930. Soviet Russia is now also focusing on the production of fuel oil. Before the war, kerosene accounted for 77% of its oil exports, gasoline accounted for 16%, and fuel oil accounted for 7%. Last year, kerosene accounted for 25.5%, gasoline accounted for 30%, and fuel oil accounted for 48%. Sales have been expanded globally, etc.

(1) (Translated from the recent German Journal of Tuberculosis) Since Dr. Koch discovered tubercle bacilli as the causative agent of pulmonary tuberculosis (i.e., consumption), scholars of tuberculosis in the East and West have been vying to study it, hoping to find a miraculous way to kill this bacterium. But the results have all been failures. This is because general physicians in the past did not understand that tubercle bacilli have a special structure. They thought that all bacteria can be eradicated with disinfectants, either by internal administration or injection, just like injecting Salvarsan for syphilis. After Dr. Bergell's painstaking research, he began to publish that tubercle bacilli have a special defense force that can resist the attacks of all external drugs. The tubercle bacillus body is composed of a neutral fat inner membrane and an acid-fast wax outer membrane (Lipoid). Unless a way is found to destroy the waxy defense line and disarm its fatty armament, there is no way to capture the tubercle bacilli and put them to death. And when tubercle bacilli attack a local part of the human body, the surrounding area is eroded to form stubborn nodules to prevent the passage of blood flow, so that the general disinfectants injected or taken internally cannot cross the Lei Chi pool. The tubercle bacilli, under these two guarantees, secretly laugh at people's inability to harm them.

Local News 2

Continued Hearing of the Xue Die Contract Termination Case

Hu Die is determined to terminate the contract. The courthouse was packed yesterday morning. Xue Die stood on opposite sides of the witness box. Lin said the contract termination was mostly not Hu's own intention. Die replied, "How do you know it wasn't my intention?" Disagreement arose sharply over goods payments and loans. Signatures and handwriting required much research. Further investigation and adjourned hearing are required. The lawsuit filed by Hu Die, a movie actress from the Star Film Company, and her fiancé Lin Xuehuai to terminate their engagement was preliminarily heard on the 28th of last month by Judge Zhou Daren of the Special District Court, who, reluctant to see a good match turn into a bad outcome, diligently ordered both parties to attempt reconciliation outside the court. In the event that restoring the old relationship proved difficult, he would conduct a continued hearing on the 20th of this month. Lin initially sent a letter through his lawyer to Hu on the 10th of this month, expressing his regret for past mistakes, while Hu, on the 14th, also replied with a letter through her lawyer, using indignant language. Since then, the two parties have engaged in a major war of words, with each letter being disclosed in this newspaper. As of yesterday, the date of the continued hearing, the two parties met again in court. Notable aspects of the court hearing are recorded below:

Crowds Inside and Outside the Courthouse. Around 8:00 AM yesterday morning, when a heavy fog enveloped the streets, the Special District Court on North Zhejiang Road was already crowded with people. Young men and women flocked to the court, many of whom had failed to secure a seat at the previous hearing and therefore arrived early this time, hoping to be among the first to enter. Since the previous hearing had been held in the Third Criminal Court, they assumed it would be the same place and crowded into the Third Court. However, when the police escorted numerous criminal cases to the court, it was suspected that the hearing would be moved to the Second Court. Unexpectedly, they all rushed upstairs, only to be turned away by the bailiffs at the Second Court. They then returned downstairs and flocked to the First Court of the High Branch, where the double doors were wide open and the lights inside were off, resembling a dark room. Seeing that it didn't look like a hearing was about to begin, the audience turned back to the Third Court. At this time, the entrance to that court was heavily guarded by bailiffs, restricting entry and exit. The crowd then gathered at the entrance, with some standing on the stairs, neither advancing nor retreating, obstructing traffic. Although the bailiffs tried to persuade them to disperse, they ignored the requests.

The Audience Surrounds Hu Die's Car. In fact, the location of the hearing had already been decided as the First Court of the High Branch, but it was feared that announcing it would cause the crowd to rush in, making it difficult to maintain order. Therefore, it was kept secret for the time being, and only the court clerk informed the lawyers and parties concerned when they arrived at the court. The general audience, unaware of the exact location, acted like madmen, shouting and rushing back and forth, which was quite amusing. After 9:00 AM, Hu Die and Lin Xuehuai, each accompanied by their lawyers, arrived at the court by car. The crowd suddenly rushed towards Hu's car, surrounding it from all sides, eager to catch a glimpse of her. As a result, Hu was unable to get out of the car. The bailiffs then dispersed the crowd, and Hu Die was able to get out with her lawyer, Zhan Jifeng. Hu's father, Shao Gong, and an old woman with white hair and a yellow fox fur collar, wearing a long robe, followed Hu Die, led by Lawyer Zhan, to the lawyers' lounge. The crowd, thinking they were going to the courtroom, also rushed over, and the entrance to the lawyers' lounge was instantly filled with people standing shoulder to shoulder. Every time a lawyer entered or exited, the bailiffs had to clear the way. Such a crowded scene was truly rare. With judicial police guarding the front and back doors. At 10:30 AM, Lawyers Eson and Ni Zheng'ao arrived in a car parked in front of the women's prison and invited their client, Lin Xuehuai, to enter the First Court of the High Branch through the side door. Hu Die, her father, and the accompanying old woman also followed Lawyer Zhan from the lawyers' lounge into the First Court. The audience tried to rush in again, but the chief of the judicial police had temporarily assigned seven or eight additional bailiffs to guard the front and back doors of the court. Despite such strict precautions, two or three hundred people still managed to squeeze in, while countless others remained outside the door. They were persuaded to disperse by the bailiffs, so there was no chaotic situation. At 11:00 AM, Judge Zhou Daren arrived in court with the court clerk and began the questioning. The hearing adjourned at 11:50 AM, with the announcement that further investigation was needed and a new hearing date would be set. The people inside the court rushed out, and those outside the court, hearing the court door creak open, suspected that the hearing was still in progress and tried to rush in, holding each other at the doorway. After another three minutes, the crowd finally realized the truth and dispersed like a tide. It can truly be said to have been an extremely grand divorce case.

Hu Die Only Seeks to Terminate the Engagement. Hu Die did not wear a hat yesterday, her hair was curled, and she wore a beige flannel coat, white gloves, and carried a coin purse. After arriving at the First Court, she sat on the right-hand side with her father and the old woman, her face solemn and without a smile. Lin Xuehuai, still in the same suit as before, sat in the back row of the lawyers' seats, only a foot away from Hu, but they did not look at each other, as if separated by a thousand miles. Judge Zhou pointed to Xue and Die, who stood on opposite sides of the witness box, and asked both parties about the progress of reconciliation after the previous adjournment. Hu Die spoke first, saying that the defendant's character, morality, and behavior were all very bad, and that reconciliation was impossible. She requested that the judge make a speedy judgment to avoid prolonged mental suffering. The judge asked her the purpose of her request, and Hu said that she only sought to terminate the engagement.

Lin Xuehuai Suffers Mentally. The judge then turned to Lin Xuehuai to ask about the reconciliation process. Lin replied that on the 10th, he had asked his lawyer to send a letter to Lawyer Zhan, requesting him to convey to the plaintiff his desire to maintain the engagement, but her reply was full of abuse, accusing him of encroaching on the car and trying to deny debts. At the end of the letter, Lawyer Zhan added that he should quickly confess the facts of his cover-ups and embellishments. He was extremely dissatisfied and felt greatly insulted. Lawyer Eson then presented the letter as evidence and said that although the defendant had been unhappy with the plaintiff before, he had sent a letter asking for her forgiveness, but the reply did not mention reconciliation at all, and instead ended with words such as "confess the facts truthfully," attacking the defendant severely. This really caused the defendant great pain.

The Reply Letter Fully Expressed Hu Die's Intention. Lawyer Zhan immediately said that the content of the reply letter fully expressed the intention of his client. The key to this case lies in the dissatisfaction with the defendant's character. Therefore, although he sincerely asked the plaintiff to reconcile, the plaintiff, because the defendant had previously written two letters, one saying "the kindness and righteousness are broken," and the other saying "terminate the engagement quickly," instructed him to write a reply asking the defendant to confess the facts of his cover-ups and embellishments to the world before reconciliation could be discussed. He then also presented the letters as evidence. The judge then asked Hu Die if the letter she replied on the 14th was her true intention, and Hu replied that it was entirely her own intention.

Hu Die Insistently Demands Termination of the Engagement. The judge then asked Lin Xuehuai that now that Hu Die was unwilling to maintain the engagement and wanted to terminate it, what was his intention? Lin replied that he knew the contract termination was mostly not Hu's own intention, so he was still unwilling to terminate it. Hu Die then said in a loud voice, "How do you know it wasn't my intention? I have already said it in court myself. How can you force me? Let alone you, no one can interfere." The judge asked Hu Die if she wanted to terminate the engagement unconditionally, and Hu said that she had suffered greatly and suffered too much loss. This small amount of compensation for the loss should be paid to her. The judge then asked Lin for his opinion, and Lin said that he still felt there was no reason to terminate the engagement. Lawyer Zhan then said that the defendant had twice expressed his desire to terminate the engagement, but now he suddenly did not want to terminate it, his intention being to avoid bearing the name of terminating the engagement.

The Problem of the Six Hundred Yuan Loan. The judge then changed the subject to the loan. First, he asked if there was evidence for the six hundred yuan loan, and Lawyer Zhan presented the check for this amount, saying that when the defendant went to the bank to withdraw the money, he had stamped the back of the check. The judge then handed the check to Lin for inspection. Lin said that the check was for him to get cash from the bank on her behalf, which he had already handed over to the plaintiff and could not prove that the money on the check was used to lend to him. He asked if there was evidence of the money being handed over. He signed the check with her as his fiancée, and he did not know that there would be today's events and did not obtain evidence. He asked if he had money deposited in the Hongkou branch of the Shanghai Bank. Lin said no. The judge turned to Hu Die and asked if she had evidence that she had lent the defendant six hundred yuan and then helped him put together five hundred taels and deposited it in the bank. Hu replied that she only saw the defendant give her a current account booklet from the Shanghai Bank, but she did not pay attention to whether the money was deposited in the branch or the head office.

The Car Price is Three Hundred and Eighty Taels. The judge then asked about the situation of the loans other than the six hundred yuan. Hu replied that the remaining money was all given in the form of checks, with the account name being "Butterfly Company." Some of the checks had a stamp, and some had her father's signature. She asked if the car was also bought with checks, and she replied yes, the car price was three hundred and eighty taels, divided into three checks, stating that the payee was Anfei Automobile Company, but the car repair costs were not included in the car price.

Goods Invoices are Evidence. The judge asked what evidence there was for the goods payments. Hu replied that it was the invoices. The judge asked if there were account books, and Hu replied that there were no account books. The judge asked who signed the invoices, and Hu replied that most of them were signed by Lin. The judge then handed the invoices to Hu and ordered her to pick out those signed by Lin. Hu replied that because she rarely saw him write, she did not recognize his handwriting very well. The judge then handed the invoices to Lin for him to read himself. Lin looked through them for a long time and said that only two of the handwriting was quite similar, but he had settled the account at the end of the month for the goods he took from the plaintiff's store and had never been in arrears. These two may have been forgotten. Lawyer Zhan then said that the defendant had previously admitted to owing more than one hundred yuan for goods, but now he was taking advantage of the plaintiff's weakness that she did not recognize his handwriting and was denying owing money. The judge then reviewed the invoices one by one and discovered that several of them were signed by Lin, but Lin said that he could not remember them one by one. If he did owe money for goods, he should produce the account books to prove it.

Taking Goods and Paying for Them Would Not Lead to Arrears. The judge then asked Hu if there was other evidence for invoices not signed by the defendant. Hu replied that she had to ask the defendant. She assumed that since he owed money, he could not deny it. Lin immediately said that the plaintiff was intentionally damaging his character and wanted to use the money owed as a tool to terminate the engagement. The judge still asked the defendant if he owed the plaintiff 185 yuan for goods. Lin replied that this amount was opened by the plaintiff, and he did not know about it, but he had paid for the goods he took and probably would not be in arrears.

It Was Said That the Loan Had to be Returned. The judge then asked about the loan to the defendant. Lin replied that the plaintiff's store was often financially strapped and could hardly lend him more than a thousand yuan. The judge also asked the plaintiff whether she had evidence regarding the loan. Hu replied that the money borrowed by the defendant was all the money she had earned, and there was no evidence. The judge asked if the 1385 yuan and 191 taels claimed were given to him for use as a fiancé and fiancée or had to be returned. Hu replied that these two amounts were loans and it was said that they had to be returned, and the money she lent him for use was not included in the calculation because there was no evidence. Lin said that this was a joke.

Xuehuai's Occupation and Salary. The judge then asked the defendant whether he had brought the newspaper that he had previously stated contained rumors of Hu Die's improper behavior. The defendant said that Zhu had brought it. Lawyer Zhan then requested the court to ask the defendant about his previous occupation and salary. Lawyer E objected and the request was denied. The judge then asked Lin if he had any other claims. Lin replied that he requested to maintain the engagement and had no other claims.

This Case Requires Further Investigation of Evidence. The judge asked where Zhou Jianyun lived, and Lin replied at the Star Film Company on Dumei Road. The judge adjourned the hearing and declared that the case required further investigation of evidence. After the investigation was confirmed, another hearing date would be set. Thus, the second act of the Xue Die marriage change came to an end.

Continuing the War of Words and Discussing Legal Principles. After returning home, the war of words continued. Because Lawyers E and Ni had replied with another letter on behalf of Lin Xuehuai the day before, they invited Ms. Hu to read it. According to reports, after reading the reply letter, she said that Die's reply was full of scolding, and after reading it, she couldn't help but laugh. After carefully reading the entire letter, the text was full of how deeply he loved, how kind, and how sincere his true love was, etc., but there was no explanation of the legal principles that cannot be separated from the word "love." Now, abandoning the word "reason" to talk about "emotion," is it because the reason is exhausted? One must know that emotion has emotion, reason has reason, and law has law. This is like a car having rails, and if it goes without them, how can it run? The provisions of Chapter 4 of the General Principles of the Civil Code regarding the expression of intent are intended to make the person expressing the intent bound by the expression of intent. If arbitrary revocation is allowed, then what is the value of this provision? This is legal principle. It is reported that when Mr. Lin is angry, he repeatedly seeks to terminate the engagement and demand compensation for damages, but suddenly he wants to maintain the old engagement and again tries to deny debts and encroach on money. His repeated words and actions are such that Die cannot bear it. Die had previously stated in a letter that she did not have time to waste words. Now, with a bone stuck in her throat, she makes a final rebuttal and entrusts this lawyer to reply, hoping that your esteemed lawyers will sincerely persuade your client to wake up quickly and not argue any further. Sincerely, Eson and Ni Zheng'ao, Barristers. Lawyer Zhan Jifeng, March 20, 20th year.

Piracy and Plunder on the Pinghu Small Ferry

Violent Pirates Pose as Passengers. The ship was raided after reaching Duxing. A shot was fired at the accountant's room. Fortunately, the injury was not serious. The Pinghu No. 1 small ferry, operated by the Pinghu Ferry Company of the Dali Wharf on Nanjing Guanqiao Bridge, which travels between Shanghai and Pinghu, was robbed by bandits around 5:00 PM the day before yesterday (the 19th) after departing from Pinghu and sailing to Shanghai via Tangkou and Zhangang. Fortunately, there were few passengers at the time, and there were no major injuries. As a result, the ship's supervisor was shot and injured in the left shin by the bandits, with losses of about a thousand yuan. The detailed circumstances are recorded below:

The Pinghu Ferry Runs Three Times a Day. There are two major companies operating small ferries between Shanghai and Pinghu, both located on the Pujiang River near Guanqiao Bridge in the Nanshi area. One is the Minnan Ferry Company of the Dashun Wharf, and the other is the Pinghu Ferry Company of the Dali Wharf. The two companies have a total of five small ferries: the Minnan, Pingshen, and Xinmin of the Minnan Company, and the Pinghu and Shanghai of the Pinghu Company. The two companies are integrated and operate in shifts three times a day, and their business is still sustainable.

More Than Ten Violent Pirates Pose as Passengers. The first shift the day before yesterday (the 19th) was the Pinghu of the Pinghu Ferry, which departed from Shanghai to Pinghu at 7:00 AM, intending to return to Shanghai at 5:30 PM, which was the earliest return shift of the day. The ship arrived in Pinghu at 11:20 AM at noon, and then set sail at 1:00 PM to return to Shanghai via Xintang, Mijing, Xuanlai Temple, Yexie, Minhang, and other ports. When the ship arrived in Minhang, more than ten violent pirates, both men and women, disguised as passengers and mixed into the ship.

Suddenly Robbery Occurred Midway. The ship was scheduled to sail directly to Shanghai after leaving Minhang. Around 4:00 PM, when the ship was sailing through the northern part of the Duxing Township and south of the Tangkou, a red light flashed in a nearby port, and a boat sped towards the ship and fired three shots to warn the ship. The pirates in the ship also took out their guns and monitored the actions of the crew members in the master cabin and engine room, and did not allow the ship to stop, but slowly sailed to avoid the eyes and ears of the river patrol. One of the pirates commanded the other pirates to start searching and robbing all the silver dollars and other items around the passengers on the ship. They were still not satisfied and wanted to strip the passengers of their clothes and transport them together with the passengers' luggage to the small boat with the red light.

Accountant Cao Jiecai Was Shot. After the pirates had robbed the passengers, they then rushed to the accounting room and asked who was the accountant. The ship's accountant, Cao Jiecai, had no way to hide and had to come out and answer, "I am." The pirate asked Cao for 5,000 yuan in cash. Cao replied that there was no cash on the ship. The pirates then threatened Cao with guns and wanted to take Cao's long robe. Cao then said to the pirates, "If you want silver dollars, I will lend you two yuan, but please don't take my clothes and make me cold." The pirates hated Cao for his cunning and fired a shot, hitting Cao's lower left leg. He immediately fell down in pain. At that time, the pirates were searching the crew members and all the rooms, and no one was spared. Even the small accounts collected by the tea room were robbed. It is estimated that the robbery lasted for about two hours and robbed more than 2,000 yuan in cash (including passengers) and countless clothes.

The Fellow Villagers Association Telephones to Request Arrest. After the pirates had finished looting, they jumped back into the small boat, fired a shot, and sped away. Afterwards, the ship's captain helped Accountant Cao Jiecai up and found that the injury was not fatal, so he immediately sailed back to Shanghai and reported the incident to the company, which then reported it to the land and water police to strictly arrest the pirates. In addition, the injured accountant Cao Jiecai was sent by car to Qu Zhibu Hospital on Penglai Road in Nanshi for treatment. Because the injury was not fatal, it was not serious. The robbed passengers then reported to the Pinghu Shanghai Fellow Villagers Association on Lingji Street in Dadongmen, Nanshi. The directors of the association, Cheng Zengfeng, Xu Qingyang, and Cui Baolu, telegraphed the Jiangsu Provincial Department of Civil Affairs yesterday, urging the Water Police Department to set a deadline to solve the case to ensure the safety of merchants and maintain the navigation industry. As for the injured accountant Cao Jiecai, he was not an employee of the Pinghu Ferry Company, but was specially dispatched by the Minnan Company to the Pinghu Ferry to supervise the ship's affairs. It is reported that the two companies have regulations in place to send people to supervise each other to prevent abuses.

British Consulate Supports the Concession's Ban on Dog Racing

From the letter of the Public Works Department to the South.

According to the *North China Daily News*, regarding the prohibition of dog racing, yesterday (19th),

The Public Works Department again exchanged letters with the British Consul General.

The British Consul General replied, expressing that the British authorities strongly supported the Public Works Department's decision to prohibit dog racing within the concession. The British Minister's view has always been that handling such matters is the responsibility of the Public Works Department.

Recently, some people who support dog racing have claimed that this type of gambling is permitted by British law. Although the British Consul General did not want to express an opinion on this point at this time, it is heard that recent cases heard in British courts have not proven that dog racing gambling is legal. In addition, Hong Kong and Singapore, British colonies, have not allowed dog racing, which is also a noteworthy point. The British authorities expressed sympathy for the Public Works Department's efforts to eliminate commercial gambling within the concession, and have long disapproved of the dog racing fields and do not want to see the British using extraterritorial rights to interfere with the Public Works Department's administration. According to the Yangjingbang Regulations, it is within the authority of the Public Works Department to regulate public entertainment venues. Since the Public Works Department has refused to issue licenses to the dog racing fields for good reason, if it now decides to order them to close, the British Minister also believes that this move is very beneficial to the concession.

Xia Xi'e's Deep Night Humiliation Involves Litigation

Two Women and One Man in a Room

Someone Snores Beside the Bed

Wang Guozhen Intends a Double Play

Wang Aizhen Knows No Shame

Xia Xi'e, a 21-year-old woman from Jiangyin residing at 2905 Nanfu Lane, Roberts Road, has recently hired a lawyer to file a complaint with the Special District Court against her fellow villager Wang Guozhen and a woman named Wang Aizhen for offenses against public morals and other matters. Yesterday afternoon, Judge Feng Shide opened the fifth court to hear the case, and both parties were present. According to Xia's statement, she was married but, due to poverty, rented a room on the front floor of Nanfu Lane with Wang Aizhen and her mother, Wang Wu. On the 23rd of the lunar December, Wang Guozhen, who claimed to be Aizhen's "older brother," wanted to stay there. On that day, Aizhen's mother, Wang Wu, was out working as a seamstress for a woman and did not return home. Aizhen proposed that she and I share a bed and let Wang Guozhen sleep alone on one bed. Because I was embarrassed to refuse Aizhen, I had to agree.

In the middle of the night, I suddenly felt that Guozhen was also lying next to Aizhen. I could not help but feel ashamed and indignant, so I got up by myself and slept on another bed. After Guozhen had a relationship with Aizhen, his lust did not subside and he crawled to my bed, trying to force himself on me and tearing at my clothes and pants. I was about to shout when Aizhen came to persuade me, saying that Wang would give me silver dollars later to buy new clothes. Although I come from a poor background, I still know etiquette and insisted on refusing, and asked Aizhen and the others to burn incense and repent the next day. Wang and the others agreed. The next morning, Wang and the others broke their promise.

I then reported the matter to the two landlords, Wang Zugen and his wife, and negotiated with them. Wang and the others then invited Zhou Jigen to mediate and were willing to pay 30 yuan as compensation. At that time, they gave Zhou 15 yuan and then gave 4 yuan the next day. On the third day, Wang and the others reported to the Putuo Road police station that Wang Zugen had been dismantling a beam, and the police arrested Zugen and sent him to court the next morning, where he was sentenced to one month of detention. But Wang's actions are really disgusting, so I filed a lawsuit. Wang Guozhen testified that on the night of December 23, he came to Shanghai to find his sister but did not find her. He went to his cousin Wang Aizhen's place to visit. Because it was late and he was unfamiliar with the area, his cousin persuaded him to stay for one night and then go to find his sister the next morning. I agreed, and Xia Xi'e and my cousin shared a bed, and I slept alone on one bed. I slept until the next morning when I went downstairs to leave, but the two landlords stopped me and accused me of molesting Xia Xi'e at night and intending to rape her.

They also gathered a crowd to imprison me and extorted 30 yuan. Because I was forced and had no way to escape, I first paid 15 yuan and then reported to the police station. I don't know Xia Xi'e at all. How could I rape her? Wang Aizhen's testimony was the same as Guozhen's, and she declared that she was a virgin and would not do anything rude.

Judge Feng said that the witness Zhou Jigen was not present today and ordered the case to be adjourned and ordered Wang Tan, the wife of the two landlords, to summon Zhou to court for questioning. Wang Guozhen paid 500 yuan for bail.

The Student's Illness is Very Serious

A Widow Files a Lawsuit

The Public Works Department's Attitude Towards the Acquisition of the Dahua Hotel

It is Inevitably Too Costly with Public Funds

It Does Not Benefit the Common People Much

The *Shanghai Evening Post* reports that the Public Works Department of the Public Concession does not want to take any action on the issue of the Dahua Hotel property at the Western Ratepayers' Annual Meeting. Unless a ratepayer proposes a motion to acquire the property as a city hall or park and it is passed by the meeting, this issue will not be raised again. According to reliable sources, the Board of Directors believes that the acquisition of the Dahua Hotel is inevitably too costly with public funds, and the result will inevitably lead to an increase in taxes. If it is converted into a park, it will only benefit the rich and not the common people much. Most directors do not agree to rebuild it into a new bureau, but if someone proposes it at the Western Ratepayers' Meeting and it is passed, the Board of Directors will not object.

Negotiations for Reprinting *The Fate of Laughter and Tears*

The Book Has Been Registered by the Ministry of the Interior

Counterfeit Books Seized in Beijing, Suzhou, Hangzhou, and Other Places

Lawsuits Have Been Filed in Local Courts

The novel *The Fate of Laughter and Tears* by Zhang Henshui was published by the Shanghai Sanyou Bookstore and exclusively sold by the Sanyi Bookstore. It has been registered by the Ministry of the Interior and issued a license No. 660 for distribution. Since its publication, it has been very popular. Recently, it was rumored that someone was privately reprinting it for profit. The company believed that since it held the copyright, it should strictly investigate. It sent people secretly to visit various ports and found that counterfeit reprints were being sold at the Zhongshan and Wulin bookstores in Hangzhou, the Xiaoshuolin and Wenyi bookstores in Suzhou, and the Capital Bookstore in Nanjing.

It immediately turned over the evidence to the police station for safekeeping and hired lawyers to file lawsuits in local courts according to law. The copperplate of the counterfeit book is blurred, the printing is poor, and the content is mostly disconnected and missing pages. The bottom page also does not have the red national emblem and copyright notice of the Sanyou Bookstore. The authenticity can be distinguished at a glance. However, the bookstores in the interior openly sell the counterfeit books for meager profits, and buyers are deceived without noticing. The reprinting is very hateful. The company, in addition to filing lawsuits in court to recover losses, will also notify special commissioners in various places to report infringements at any time to protect the copyright. It will also publish warnings in newspapers to warn all bookstores not to lightly attempt to print and sell counterfeit books.

May 1st and May 5th

The Central News Agency reports that the Shanghai Municipal Government has raised questions regarding the ambiguity of the Central Executive Committee's amended regulations on factory holidays, specifically regarding whether or not May 5th should be a holiday,

National Federation of Commerce Cables for Dredging of the Yangtze River

Yesterday, the National Federation of Chambers of Commerce sent separate telegrams to the National Government Construction Committee in Nanjing, the Yangtze River Conservancy Commission, the Hubei Provincial Government Water Conservancy Bureau in Wuchang,

and other relevant bodies, stating, "Recently, we received a letter from nine groups, including the Yiyang and Yangxin

Chambers of Commerce in Hubei, which stated that the Great River, also known as the Yangtze River, flows from Sichuan into Hubei, from Yisha to Xinghekou, converging with the water from Dongting Lake in Hunan and reaching Xindi. Its source is mixed,

carrying silt. Numerous ships pass through, depositing coal ash. In addition, due to historical changes,

the embankments have been increasing daily, with farmers competing with the water surface for land. The river's shape has changed from a bowl

to a saucer, and the shallow water has caused silt to accumulate, forming islands. This is inevitable. Forty-five li upstream of Xindi is Luoshan. During the Qing Xianfeng and Tongzhi periods, it was a town with convenient river and lake access.

Later, due to river siltation, it became a dead port. In the river at Xindi,

there is only a line of sandbars. In recent years, the area has gradually

increased, starting from Zhujia and extending to Maobu Township, spanning more than forty li, dividing the river surface between Xindi and Jiayu County on the opposite bank into two sections, including Zhou,

Qingjiang Estuary and other places. The riverbed is silting up, and the islands are winding. During high water, the slightest carelessness may lead to grounding. If it is autumn or winter,

when the water is low, even small vessels have difficulty navigating. Military vessels and merchant ships are out of the question. Therefore,

last winter, a small boat from Xiantao capsized upstream of Xindi at Daoling.

The Jiali merchant ship ran aground on the old river surface opposite Xindi. Such incidents are too

numerous to count. At this time, with the beginning of political tutelage and the vigorous suppression of bandits, the throat of the Great River, connecting

Sichuan and Hunan above and reaching Nanjing and Shanghai below, is being allowed to be blocked by islands and silt. Not only will

Xindi become a second Luoshan, trapped in eternal ruin, but also the obstruction of the waterway will affect the commerce of Sichuan, Hunan, Hubei, Jiangxi, Anhui, Jiangsu, and Zhejiang provinces and cities. Moreover,

in the event of a major military emergency, military vessels will have difficulty passing through, making it difficult for neighboring provinces to move troops to rescue each other,

like the head and tail of a Changshan snake responding to each other. This is still speaking of the inconvenience of transportation. If there is a flood,

causing a disaster and turning the land into a swamp, as far back as the Wushen and Jiyou years [1908, 1909] and as recently as the Yimao and Bingyin years [1927, 1928], dikes and embankments will be breached, fields will be flooded, and houses will be swept away. The lives and property of the people

will be eliminated by the giant waves. Although national funds are spent on relief, foreign loans

can never restore vitality. The reason is that the river is not dredged and is silting up day by day. Without this solution, even if we talk about construction every day,

it is like not grasping the root and only managing the branches. In the blink of an eye, the market towns will be flooded, the fields will be submerged, and the people will be displaced. What is called construction is like the hair without the skin, where can it be attached?

This is another meaning of the Great River's impact on water disasters. The late Premier Sun Yat-sen's teachings on dredging the river were detailed and insightful, and many can be verified.

We, the public groups, live in Xindi, and we are shocked by what we see. Regarding the interests and harms of this Great River, which are related to national planning and the people's livelihood, how can we remain silent? In addition to submitting separate reports to the National Government Construction Committee, the Hubei Provincial Government, and the Water Conservancy Bureau, we

hereby submit a document requesting that your association approve the transfer to various officials to send personnel to the Xindi

area along the river to conduct detailed surveys and regular dredging to promote water conservancy and strengthen

the foundation of the country. It is for the public good." Upon investigation, the dredging of the Great River is a matter of great importance.

We respectfully and unanimously advocate for appealing and calling for action to form a consensus and facilitate implementation. We await your reply.

The Chairman of the National Federation of Chambers of Commerce, Lin Kanghou, and Standing Committee Members Su Minsheng, Zhang Yuquan, Lu Guangji, Chen Riping, Li Kuian, and Peng Chuli, respectfully kowtow and stamp.

Zhu Qinglan's Talks on Reclamation in Huainan

Presenting Three Strategies

Mr. Zhu Ziqiao [Zhu Qinglan] has come to Shanghai to raise funds for disaster relief in Shaanxi. All sectors believe in his sincerity

and effectiveness in relieving disasters. Therefore, they have welcomed him and assisted in fundraising daily. In less than two weeks, he has already obtained a donation of 100,000 yuan. His enthusiasm for disaster victims and his credibility in society

are beyond description. Reporters from various newspapers knew that Mr. Zhu and Mr. Zhang Jian of Nantong were proponents of the Huainan salt pan reclamation project

and that he was also the chairman of a certain salt reclamation company. In recent years, the Huainan reclamation industry has long been doubted by society,

so they took advantage of Mr. Zhu's busy schedule to ask for his opinion. His remarks

should be welcomed by those who care about industry. They are disclosed as follows:

(Question) Sir, you have made great contributions to disaster relief in North China. I heard that you have been involved in reclamation

in Jiangbei. Have you paid attention to it in recent years? What is the situation now?

(Answer) The disaster area is too vast, and the disaster is too severe. We can only say that we have done our best, according to our conscience, to judge.

There are still many people who cannot be rescued, so how can we talk about merit? As for reclaiming the Jiangbei salt pans, I followed Mr. Zhang Si [Zhang Jian] and organized the

Huacheng Salt Reclamation Company. Later, I joined forces with friends to establish the Taihe Salt Reclamation Company. Taihe has been progressing steadily. Although it has not made a profit, it can still be sustained. Huacheng, on the other hand, made the mistake of having too little capital budget and the mistake of having chaotic steps taken by those in charge, resulting in

interruption midway. At this time, no one responded to increasing shares, and no one believed in lending money.

The only option is to maintain the status quo and wait for the opportune time. We also plan to submit all the land

to the government authorities as an experimental area for equal land ownership. Whether it can be implemented is still uncertain. Although I have not been personally involved in the company's affairs in recent years,

I have entrusted my most trusted friend, Mr. Zhang Peiyan, to be my representative. All matters are discussed by letter and telegram. Therefore, many difficult problems have been solved satisfactorily over the years.

If the company has a solution that can slightly reduce the disaster in North China, I will definitely go to Jiangbei to continue the work and will never be one who starts but does not finish.

(Question) The salt reclamation companies are all about ten years old or more, and the capital is hundreds of thousands or even millions, but we have not heard of any success. Why is it so difficult to operate this industry?

(Answer) Coastal land is formed by seawater accumulation, and its geological

evolution is slower than that of plains and mountains. The various methods of changing the geology

cannot be explained in a short time. However, because there is a certainty of improvement,

and because the region is in a densely populated area of Jiangsu Province with a mild climate,

the unprofitable or indebted state of the various companies engaged in operations has its own differences. However, regarding inadequate capital, incomplete projects,

inadequate equipment, and unfavorable environment, resulting in hindered progress and poor harvest,

the problems are almost the same. If we understand this, we will know that it is not that this industry cannot be done, but that there are various preventive factors such as timing, environment, and resources.

(Question) In your opinion, what measures should be taken to promote the success of the Jiangbei reclamation industry?

(Answer) The coastal area of Huainan, located east of the Fan Gong Dike, is no less than

ten million mu. With such a vast area, if the state were to operate it, like the Song Dynasty building dikes and constructing sluices along the coast,

this area of land could have long been transformed into fertile land. However, the authorities at that time did not consider this, so Mr. Zhang Si took the initiative to do it with private funds. Regardless of the difficulty in raising funds and the layers of obstacles,

the working plans were not unified, and the work was already illegal. Moreover, after various obstacles and setbacks, the situation of today was created.

In my opinion, there should be the following measures:

(1) The state should raise large sums of money to build dikes that have not yet been built along the coast, build sluices that should be built, and open trunk rivers that should be opened, so that the people can enjoy water conservancy. After the reclamation matures, either collect additional project fees or collect project fees together with the increased tax.

The people will enjoy the benefits, and the government funds will be repaid. This is a comprehensive planning approach.

The people will benefit from reclamation, and the public funds will be repaid. This is the best policy.

(2) If it is difficult to raise large sums of money and large-scale projects cannot be undertaken, then the existing companies should be given financial assistance separately, and personnel should be sent to supervise the money to ensure that it is not wasted and that the unfinished projects are completed.

The assistance should be given with a long-term repayment period. This is an approach that takes advantage of the situation.

The companies' previous efforts will not be abandoned, and there will be considerable results in the future. This is the next best policy.

(3) If the state does not have time for this at this time, then bandits should be eliminated to allow people to settle down and work, and taxes should be reduced to reduce the burden. This is a policy of recuperation.

Although there will not be rapid progress, there will be gradual progress. This is the minimum requirement. If even this cannot be achieved, how can we promote the success of the reclamation industry?

However, I still have one heartfelt word to offer to you, sir. When Mr. Zhang Si and I were engaged in the Jiangbei reclamation industry, the purpose was not to seek large profits for the shareholders, but to open up sources of profit for the local area.

It is hoped that all construction will be based on this development. Otherwise, the precedent of the reclamation and pastoral company is there. Who would be willing to invest for more than ten years without receiving interest? The world still regards them as large capital landowners, and their views are inevitably wrong.

Six Records of the Burning of the Daji Steamer

The Actual Number of Fatalities Exceeds Two Hundred and Fifty

The case of the Daji steamer of the Da Da Steamer Company, which was sailing to Zhanghuanggang and caught fire due to carelessness,

has been reported in previous issues. However, as of yesterday, it has been reported that the number of crew members and passengers who died in the disaster

has exceeded two hundred and fifty. The following is a record of the news received yesterday.

Hull Repair: The hull of the Daji was towed back to Shanghai by Chu Heng at approximately 5:00 PM on the 17th.

In the evening, it entered the Ruirong Shipyard in Yangshupu for repairs. Before entering the shipyard, the Water Patrol Team dispatched police officers

to inspect the ship together with the Navigation Association and the Customs River Authority. In addition to the remaining ashes, there were

five iron barrels containing salt. Because they were securely placed, they were not burned.

The shipyard has now refreshed and cleaned the hull and is surveying the bottom of the ship in preparation for repairs. The total repair cost is estimated to be more than 100,000 yuan.

Actual Number of Fatalities: Yesterday, a reporter from Guowen Newspaper investigated from various sources.

The number of crew members and passengers who died in this disaster is more than two hundred. The Daji

steamed from Shanghai through the major ports of Tongzhou and other ports. Some passengers boarded the ship without purchasing tickets,

and there were also free passengers and hawkers, making it impossible to verify the numbers. Therefore,

the number of bodies recovered by sandboats and company-dispatched salvage vessels in recent days

has already reached two hundred and sixty-seven or eight. Approximately

twenty or thirty more people are missing and have not yet been found. Therefore, the total number in the future will be between two hundred and seventy and three hundred.

Three More Coffins Arrive: For several days, boats have been transporting coffins back. The first

batch of eight coffins and the second batch of thirteen coffins all belonged to crew members and passengers who lived in Jiangnan.

On the 19th and 20th, Daqing and Dahe arrived in Shanghai, transporting three more coffins: (1) Li Asheng, head of the kitchen, from Zhoushan; (2) Pan Boqing, cook, from

Lanxi; (3) Passenger Zhou Dayin, whose family is in Shanghai, so they were temporarily placed in the Huaiyang Guild Hall. Yesterday, most of the coffins of the crew members who died in the disaster were transported back to their hometowns

on the Xinning Shaolun.

Continuing Reports: For several days, the Chonghai Fellow Countrymen's Association has been registering

the names of the deceased and missing persons. Some relatives were late due to delays en route, while others returned to Shanghai after searching in vain at the scene of the accident.

The association facilitates investigation. Therefore,

more relatives came in the past two days. The surnames are recorded on the left.

Company's Aftermath: For several days, the Dada Company has been holding board meetings

to discuss the aftermath. The details are complex and inconsistent between people and goods. The communications department has also consulted with the Jianghai Customs Supervision Office for investigation. Yesterday, the company submitted a document

explaining its aftermath plans. It is reported that the general approach can be divided into three parts: cargo and passenger losses. The company will consult with the Navigation Association to determine the amounts for freight losses. Crew members

will be compensated by the company. Passengers are registered and verified, and the company will consult with the fellow countrymen's association to handle the situation. The amounts are still being discussed and cannot be determined.

It is feared that it will take several more days.

City Public Works Bureau to Examine Automobile Drivers' Licenses

Starting April 1st

The City Public Works Bureau registers each automobile driver in the city and issues a driver's

license. Originally, examinations were conducted every full year. However, because the dates on which drivers

received their licenses varied, they often could not remember the dates later on. Therefore, it was revised

to designate April 1st to June 30th of each year as the license examination period to

standardize and facilitate memorization. Now that the period is not far off, it is reported that the bureau has begun

preparing the license examination procedures. It is also reported that if an automobile driver does not submit their license

to the bureau for examination, they will be fined five yuan if they are overdue for less than one month, and their license

will be revoked if they are overdue for more than one month.

Movie Theater Almost Sued for Not Paying Stamp Tax

Since the French Concession stamp tax has been handled by Specialists Liu Chunyuan and Shen Rulin,

they have simultaneously implemented both promotion and exhortation to drive sales and tax collection achievements are constantly improving. And even the rental revenue stamps have been gradually implemented. Regarding entertainment venues

and vehicle stamps, there has been a vigorous overhaul to eliminate favoritism. This is because it was found

that the French Concession movie theaters have been observing, delaying, and resisting filling out business forms and stamp tax payments monthly. The delay has been four months. Liu

and Shen submitted a report to the Jiangsu Stamp Tax and Liquor and Tobacco Office in Shanghai,

which sent a letter to the French Concession Patrol House. The patrol house immediately dispatched officer

Guo, an employee of the movie theater, for a stern warning. He was given three days to pay the back taxes

to the French Concession Stamp Tax Office. If he could provide written proof that he had complied, he would be exempt from prosecution. Otherwise,

he would be prosecuted according to the law. After receiving the order, Guo went to the French Concession Stamp Tax Office in Zhenping Lane

and pleaded repeatedly. He promised to pay the taxes owed for the four months of November, December, January, and February and to file reports and pay taxes monthly in the future.

Liu and Shen were invited to approve the matter leniently

and sent a letter to the General Patrol House to withdraw the charges and express their gratitude for the assistance. The movie theater's warning will serve as a precedent for other entertainment venues.

Judgment on the Registration Rights of the Little Luzon Tobacco Factory

Little Luzon's Old Beauty and Comet brand cigars have long been popular

and sold in China for more than forty years. It has recently been reported that

there are similar products in Hong Kong. The British government has ruled that the registration rights should belong exclusively to the Little

Luzon Tobacco Factory and that others cannot use them concurrently.

Trade Association News

Soy and Rice Industry：Soy and Rice Industry Association convened a special meeting of the North and South rice merchants yesterday to reorganize trade regulations. Present were over two hundred and forty people, including Ye Huijun, Zhu Zixiang, Yan Xiaoquan, Cai Yukun, Lu Jingwen, Fu Qiangeng, etc. The meeting started at 2 PM, with Chairman Ye Huijun reporting the purpose of the meeting. Zhu Zixiang, Fu Qiangeng, Cai Yukun, and Lu Jingwen subsequently proposed and the meeting resolved the following matters: (1) Commissions will remain as before, with a deduction of 22 cents (洋二角二分) per stone (石) from the customer's commission. For cash transactions on the shop's side, a rebate of 6 cents will be given, and for monthly settlements, a rebate of 4 cents will be given. Checks will generally not be accepted. If checks must be used by reputable shops, they must be stamped to be exchanged for bank notes (莊票), to prevent the bank notes from being swapped. Checks from other shops will be uniformly rejected. (2) If a reputable shop's check has been stamped for exchange into bank notes, but the bank refuses to exchange it, then the North and South offices should be immediately notified to inform the trade, and transactions should only be conducted after receiving the payment. (3) After this reorganization of trade regulations, if any member intends to disrupt them, fellow traders may report anonymously to the North and South offices, which will convene the trade to severely deal with the matter. The meeting adjourned after 5 PM.

Restaurant Industry: The Restaurant Industry Association held its twelfth executive committee meeting on March 19th. Chairman Cheng Kefan reported on incoming correspondence and then discussed the following matters: (A) A letter from the Municipal Chamber of Commerce regarding a donation drive for the Shaanxi disaster relief emergency fund, along with the organizing rules and a list of donors. It was resolved to submit it to the next executive committee for review and to notify all members for their information. (B) Regarding the issue of supervisors (監察委員) in the Trade Association, the Trade Association Law does not explicitly provide for it but does not prohibit it. It was resolved that the Trade Association's regulations should freely define this matter. (C) A letter from the Municipal Chamber of Commerce regarding the organization of a joint technical research department by various trade associations. It was resolved to file it. (D) The Social Bureau's approval of the reported use of the seal and the destruction of the old Chamber of Commerce seal was approved for filing. The rest is omitted. The meeting adjourned at slightly after 6 PM.
