Free Talk

World Anecdotes

— Sea Wanderer

▲In Persia, it is considered shameful for men to laugh, because everyone believes that laughter belongs to women. Therefore, when they feel like laughing, they often force themselves not to. However, women can laugh as they please without any reservation.

▲Madagascar, an island east of South Africa, is a French colony. Silk is the cheapest clothing material on the island. Therefore, even the poorest women wear silk clothes.

▲In recent years, postcards have become popular all over the world. But the first country to use postcards was Austria.

▲The sand in the Sahara Desert in Africa is, on average, about thirty feet deep.

▲According to research by a British naturalist, a grasshopper can jump two hundred times the length of its body. A spider eats twenty-seven times its body weight every day.

▲In Iceland, north of Britain, men have the custom of kissing each other when they meet. But they rarely kiss women.

▲There are as many as 250,000 species of flowering plants produced in the British islands.

▲There are several places in Mexico that are arid year-round and never experience rain.

▲A very famous aviator in England has an insurance policy of 200,000 pounds and must pay an annual premium of 60,000 pounds.

Anecdotes of Coal Hill

— Qing Qu

March 19th is the anniversary of Emperor Sizong of Ming's death on Coal Hill. The old calendar has been abolished, so this day coincides with the revolution of the seventy-two martyrs of Huanghuagang on March 29th. I remember that in the past, people commemorated Sizong by attributing it to the birth of the sun, hence the beginning of their scripture: "The sun is bright, the light of Zhu Buddha," which is understandable.

People only know that in the year of Jia Shen (1644), the rebel Li Zicheng entered Xi'an. When he was about to cross the river, Li Jiantai was the supervisor who was supposed to suppress the bandits. Emperor Sizong personally went to Zhengyang Gate, held a cup, and said to him, "Sir, go forth as if I were going." However, before long, the troops retreated. Since then, cities fell one after another, not only Pingyang and Taiyuan. Moreover, in a conversation, the eunuch Du Xun had already surrendered to the rebels. Yet, the ministers of the capital, such as Wei Zhaode, remained silent. After the deaths of Xiong Tingbi and Yuan Chonghuan, it can be said that there was no one in the court. Therefore, when Emperor Sizong was dying, he said, "The monarch is not the one who brought about the downfall of the country, but the ministers are," referring to this.

After the year of Ren Wu (1642), the northern troops arrived at Heyang. Even before the western bandits invaded, the capital was already in danger. The only thing to rely on for defense was the Beijing Garrison, but its numbers were insufficient. Moreover, the city wall had more than 54,000 sections. The emperor knew that it could not be defended, so he ordered all the eunuchs below the seal-holding eunuchs of various supervisorates, regardless of age, to ascend the wall. After a long time, because there was no cooking, the so-called defending soldiers all left their posts to look for food. Meanwhile, rebellious eunuchs like Cao Huachun had long been in communication with the rebels. Even if there were loyalist troops, they could not protect an inch of land. Moreover, there was no one who could lead troops to rush to the rescue.

During the Wanli reign (1573-1620), taxes were already heavy, and the people suffered. But by the end of the Chongzhen reign (1628-1644), the various levies of the past, such as the Liaodong levy and the bandit suppression levy, could not be collected. On the first day of the Jia Shen year, the ministers reported to the emperor that the border defense expenses were heavy and there was no way to pay for them, and they all requested from the imperial treasury. The emperor was reluctant. Then, he tearfully summoned the Vice Minister of Revenue Wu Luzhong and asked if there was any silver in the treasury. Wu replied, "Only eighty thousand taels." Unable to do anything else, the emperor urged the officials to donate to the military expenses. The Earl of Jiading, Zhou Kui, who was also the father of Empress Zhou, possessed vast wealth but did not donate a single coin. Emperor Sizong subtly hinted to the Empress, and she poured out what she had stored in the palace to give to Kui, hoping he would understand the emperor's intention. However, Kui swallowed half of it and presented the rest. Yet, there was an old man, already sixty years old, who had never held an official position in the court, who cried bitterly and donated four hundred taels, accumulated from his blood and sweat. To say that there was no one who loved the country would be an inaccurate assertion. Alas, this is why I cannot stop writing after reading the last page of the Ming History.

Lament for the Passing of Tang Meixi, a Master of Poetry, Due to a Love Suicide in the Moon Palace—I Only Learned of It From Shoujuan

— Tao Zaidong

Meixi's amorous nature has withered away,

Wind and rain grieve for his literary talent.

Cuckoos cry in the clear moonlight,

Unbearable to re-examine the purple orchids.

The tragedy of the grieving woman is pitiable,

Her intelligence deceived, missing her best time.

A true romantic soul in this world,

Regretting not meeting before she was married.

Arrows cluster, dividing the fields,

There are no good matches in this world.

The old poet understands the emptiness of beauty,

Yet still sheds a tear for the radiant red.

The drama of the resentful woman and infatuated man is heartbreaking,

How much karmic debt is hard to repay.

A passionate admonition to arrange,

Seventy-two lovebirds, thirty-six lines.

Record of a Boy Scout Patriotic Speech

— Ms. Ye Hua

It is said that General Baden-Powell founded the Boy Scouts, originally emphasizing civic and national training for children. Our country's Boy Scouts began in the second year of the Republic. Now, under the guidance of the Party, they are making greater efforts toward the goal of national training. The Shanghai Boy Scouts held the first Patriotic Speech Competition on the anniversary of Sun Yat-sen's death. This is an unprecedented grand event for our country's Party-affiliated Boy Scouts. I will record a few things I saw and heard to leave a trace.

▲Wang Jie's Anxiety: Wang Jie, a girl scout, won first place in the middle school group. This is a new era since our country started girl scouts in the fifth year of the Republic. Her main characterstic is liveliness, preferring movement to stillness. The order of speeches was based on the order of reports, and Wang's speech happened to be scheduled last. Watching her comrades take the stage one by one, she looked forward with anticipation, but it never seemed to be her turn. She was in a state of anxiety and impatience, like a tiger entering a cage for the first time, unsure of what to do with its hands and feet, then with her blood rising, her face flushed. Finally, she muttered the words of her speech. I sat beside her, seeing her anxiety, I felt anxious for her too. My heart was very uneasy. When the judging ended, Wang was actually ranked at the top. At this point, we suddenly realized that Wang Jie's anxiety was not without reason.

▲Yellow Clothing Psychology: After the photography was finished, someone asked why a certain Boy Scout was wearing a yellow hat and yellow clothes, almost everything on him was yellow. Someone said, "Preference for color varies according to ethnicity and individual. People tend to love the red and yellow ends of the light spectrum. Yellow is the most prominent color in the light spectrum, making people active and encouraged. In our country's feudal era, commoners favored red, and nobles favored yellow. Yellow was more honored than red. The emperor's clothes were called yellow robes, and edicts were copied on yellow paper, called yellow lists. The ground the emperor passed was paved with yellow earth, and from the roof tiles to the cushions, everything was yellow. During the Qing dynasty, even the national flag was yellow, members of the imperial family wore golden yellow belts, and ministers wore yellow mandarin jackets. It can be said that yellow reached its peak. Also, in ancient times, 'green clothes and yellow skirt' meant that the concubine was valued more than the wife, reversing the proper order of status. How noble is the color yellow! No wonder Boy Scouts love yellow. However, the yellow of the Boy Scouts has no noble or superstitious meaning, but only takes its active and encouraging aspects, using this to strive and forge ahead."

▲Iron Discipline: The competition was divided into group and individual. It was originally stipulated that each Boy Scout group should select two representatives to participate. However, this provision was dropped from the regulations due to a printing error. The only way to remedy this was to issue a notice. However, the notice said that two representatives should be selected, but mistakenly wrote "two people maximum," which was different from the original intention. The oral report beforehand stated that two people were the standard. But some people did not hear about it, so there were groups with one or two people present. This matter was quickly brought to the judging panel. The result was based on the written words, meaning that "two people maximum" meant at most two people could participate, one was acceptable, but three was not. Fortunately, the scores of the one person were sometimes lucky and sometimes unlucky, which was very fair. So, one person was allowed to represent the group. After the judging was completed, the winning group in one group was represented by one person, and those who had two people present could not help but feel disappointed. However, they could only obey the decision without any objection. Such discipline is worthy of praise. Disputes in competition arenas are common both at home and abroad, and have become commonplace. This competition had room for dispute, but no one disputed it, which is a deep demonstration of the Boy Scouts' virtues.

On Fan Fanshan

— Zheng Yimei

Mr. Fan Fanshan passed away on the fourteenth of this month. Heaven was unwilling to spare him, and an elder statesman has withered away. A poetry master of his generation, his elegant style has faded. The birds sing in sorrow. Mr. Fan was a resident of the capital for many years. Surrounded by chaos and political turmoil, Mr. Fan, along with Luo Yinggong, Yi Longyang, and others, composed poetry and drank wine, forgetting the world. After Luo and Yi went to heaven one after another, Mr. Fan felt quite lonely. His body was originally healthy, but in recent years he gradually showed signs of aging. Last year, he accidentally ate "Ma Da Gun" (馬打滚) and fell ill. "Ma Da Gun" is a local food from Jiangxi province. It is made by steaming glutinous rice flour until cooked, then shaping it into a cake. After it dries and hardens, it is cooked in water until it becomes porridge. It is called "Zi Ba" (粢粑). Then, sugar frost and bean and wheat flour are taken and placed in a bowl. The Zi Ba is put into the bowl, and the sugar frost and bean and wheat flour naturally adhere to it. It tastes sweet and delicious. It is called "Ma Da Gun" because of its shape. But his aging and weak stomach could not digest it, causing him to be bedridden for many days. Therefore, there were rumors outside that Mr. Fan had passed away. It was an inaccurate rumor about "Dongpo of the Overseas." Mr. Fan laughed it off. Mr. Fan had a romantic and beautiful nature. Even in his later years, he still liked to compose poems about beauties, giving the impression of a glance behind a fan, captivating all. His depictions of feelings were like paintings, enchanting and unforgettable to read. My friend Xu Ziya admired his poetic talent and treated him with the respect due a teacher. At that time, the game of poetry riddles was popular in Shanghai. Ziya often went to ponder them. One day, the riddle was a poem by Fan Fanshan. Ziya was very familiar with his poems, so he wrote the answer. He also copied the answers of others and concentrated them in his own. When the answer was revealed, it was indeed Ziya who got it right. He won four hundred gold coins, which was a wonderful story at the time. Senior Zhang Danweng has a small portrait of Mr. Fan that was given to him. I had the opportunity to see it. He looked thin and dignified, wearing formal attire and thick-soled court boots. It was probably taken when he was an official during the Qing dynasty. Mr. Fan's documents and letters have already been published. His remaining poems number over 30,000, and someone will soon publish them. In the early years of the Republic of China, Mr. Fan often submitted his poems to newspapers for publication. I also loved to read Mr. Fan's poems and would record and save them whenever I saw them. I still have one or two handwritten copies in my travel bag, all of which are Mr. Fan's masterpieces. Mr. Fan passed away at the age of eighty-six.

Epitaph for the Late Mrs. Wang

— Hu Yuan of Xiangtan

The deceased Mrs. Wang, whose given name was Jian, and courtesy name was Yunxiang, came from a Wang family originally from Shanyin, Zhejiang. During the Qing Jiaqing and Daoguang eras, they came to Hunan and settled in Changsha. Her father's name was Benchang, and her mother was Madam Tong. Madam Tong was widowed early and had two children, whom she raised and taught according to proper etiquette. Mrs. Wang followed her mother and was raised by her grandmother (玉母), known for her filial piety and careful selection of a spouse. She married Yuan Shuo as his second wife at the age of twenty-seven. Yuan Shuo's family was poor and did not engage in production. After returning from studying in Japan in the Guangxu Renyin year, he was distressed by the precarious state of the country and founded the Mingde School. For more than twenty years since then, he was constantly traveling abroad, not returning home for the entire year. Even when he did return, he did not have time to rest, constantly seeking solutions. He entrusted all the affairs within the family to Mrs. Wang and did not concern himself with them. Mrs. Wang managed everything calmly. With refined elegance and high moral standards, she wore simple clothes and ate simple food, avoiding servants and maids, and operating with ease. The room rarely had hidden savings, and the pantry was often empty, but nothing was left undone. Gifts from relatives and parties were always properly distributed. Yuan Shuo was able to focus on running the school, and people also recognized that Mrs. Wang was virtuous because the Yuan family lived so plainly and was able to endure hardships. Mrs. Wang had no worldly desires, but only loved reading books. She held a book in her hand every day, forgetting the cold and heat. Her poems, lyrics, and parallel prose were mostly worth preserving. Yuan Tan once recorded them in a volume called "Late Sunny Collection." She also had several handwritten "Admonitions to My Sons," based on morality and offering comprehensive and insightful advice, with many words that could be emulated. In her later years, she devoted herself to Buddhism, and her temperament became even more tranquil. She was taciturn and rarely spoke. Although her body was weak and prone to illness, she would always conceal her illness and avoid causing trouble. This summer, she passed away from a minor illness a few days before the Xiang turmoil began. At that time, Yuan Tan was in Beijing, and was unable to return home due to the chaos. Alas! Mrs. Wang was born on the twenty-eighth day of the eighth month of the Guiyou year of the Qing Tongzhi reign and died on the fifth day of the fifth month of the Gengwu year of the Republic, at the age of fifty-eight. She had three sons: Mu, who studied economics at Keio University in Japan and obtained a bachelor's degree, marrying Zhang; Yi, who studied education at the University of Chicago in the United States and obtained a doctorate, marrying Shuai; and Zheng, who was enrolled in the National Conservatory of Music and was engaged to Chen. She had one granddaughter. She was buried on a Wushen day in the mid-winter of this year, at the original site of Shiguchou in Daxian Town, Changsha, facing Yi (乙) in the first direction and Xin (辛) in the foot direction. The inscription reads:

Oh, virtuous spouse, truly my good friend.

She was as composed as a quiet maiden, as industrious as a weaver woman.

Frugal yet adhering to propriety, possessing substance with elegance.

Her words formed chapters, praising her pure virtue.

How could it be that one day, she would rest forever?

If it weren't for the turmoil, who would have known Buddha's power?

Her radiant beauty is concealed, her clear zither's sound is left behind.

This stone records her chastity, and my heart is filled with sorrow.

Random Musings on Europe (6)

— Wang Yachen

Among the works of French masters in this museum, the four large murals by Chavannas are particularly noteworthy. They are embedded in the four walls next to the three-story escalator. Each mural is about thirty feet long and five feet wide. Not only are the depictions solid, but the subjects are also very meaningful. The first mural depicts the era of Greece, depicting the glorious scene of ancient Greek art. The background is filled with characters from Greek mythology. The second mural depicts the Roman era, depicting the glory of the Roman era, dominated by magnificent Roman architecture. The figures in the painting are all nude, enjoying a sense of natural intoxication, expressed vividly. The third mural depicts the era of religion, depicting the glorious scene of religious art. A group of believers are making murals in a church, evoking the sincerity of that time towards religion. The architecture in the painting all uses Roman-style arches, which immediately show the greatness of the Roman religious era. These three murals were made in 1885. There is another mural by the door, depicting the first ancestors of mankind, Adam and Eve, forming a decorative pattern of symmetrical shapes. The color and composition are elaborately designed. The above four works are truly Chavannas's best works. To the left of Chavannas's murals is a large room displaying Italian and French paintings from the Renaissance to the end of the 18th century, totaling more than a hundred pieces. Among them is a nude woman by Robert Sterl, whose technique of applying color is very similar to Tie Qing (Titian). This is the best Italian painting in the room. Besides this, the Italian paintings displayed are not masterpieces. Among them are several copies by great French painters, which are worth noting. 1. Manet's copy of Delacroix's "Dante's Boat," originally number 200, is displayed in the Louvre Museum in Paris. Manet only used a number 6 canvas for the sea, but he was able to express most of the feeling. 2. Delacroix's copy of Correggio's "Holy Image," originally an eighty-figure work, is also displayed in the Louvre Museum in Paris. Delacroix used a small number 5 canvas to copy its general human figures and clothes, all of which had the same feeling as the original. The skill of the technique and the depth of the color are impeccable. 3. Delacroix's copy of Tie Qing's famous "Descent from the Cross," the painting is only number 6, but it does not lose the spirit of Tie Qing's original work. In the past, all the great painters in Europe, during their exploratory period, lingered in the Louvre Museum in Paris, conducting in-depth studies of the works of ancient masters. In the past, those who copied paintings only followed the general outline of the original work and used their own techniques. Copying according to this method is indeed of great benefit to one's own technique. Writers whose basic conditions of their own technique have already been resolved will not be confused by the original work when copying ancient paintings. Seeing the copies by Manet and Delacroix, I feel that the work of copying paintings is meaningful. After visiting the paintings upstairs, I went downstairs again and saw sculptures displayed, totaling more than ten rooms. There are many famous Italian sculptures and reproductions. Although they are not as precious as the famous Italian sculptures, they are enough for art lovers to study. After the sculpture room, I went upstairs and saw modern French works displayed. Each of the famous painters in Paris has one or two works displayed. The museum must close at noon. By the time I finished visiting, it was almost noon, and I had not had time to record everything. I left the museum and took a car back to the vicinity of the British hotel for lunch. After lunch, I strolled along the river. The background of the river is mountains, and the trees are neatly planted on both banks. Looking into the distance, the houses are densely packed, and the prosperity is no less than Paris. There are more ships sailing in the river than in the Seine in Paris. Because the area is commercially prosperous, the transportation is also more lively. I walked along the river for four or five miles and then returned to the hotel for a short rest. I took the special express train back to Paris at 3:14 PM.

Gold Speculation Returns to a Weak Path

America Has News of a Silver Famine Relief

High Winds and Rough Waves: Extreme Danger: Gold speculation on March 20th once again took a weak turn, with extreme and unpredictable ups and downs. The difference between the opening and closing prices was seventeen or eighteen taels, causing extreme nervousness. The result was a sharp drop of thirteen taels, although the exchange rate continued to shrink by half a point, the internal market was already flooded. This was truly a divergent trend of external tightness and internal looseness. The prices of spot market trades were very different. In the morning, Yuan Maoyong, Tong Taichang, Xin Heng, etc., were all buyers, while Chang Sheng Yong, Qian Changxiang, Cui Changyong, etc., mostly sold. Overseas silver markets all reported declines, but the gold price instead fell. The reason for this was that America seemed to have the intention of relieving the silver famine, as well as the stimulation of the Japanese cabinet turmoil. Afterwards, the ups and downs of over ten taels near 700 taels became unbearable. In the afternoon market, prices were initially stable, then weakened, as the selling pressure was very strong. With the increasing supply of bills of exchange, prices plummeted by more than ten taels, almost to the point of collapse, finally breaking the 690-tael mark. The British gold price has settled at four pence, which has become a stable situation in recent days. However, both long and short positions are very dangerous. The spot market also seemed to soften, with a premium of about eight taels for term trading.

The Market Opened with a Drop and Became Complicated: The May contract opened in the morning with a drop of five taels, at 698 taels. The long-term price fell by sixteen and nine-sixteenths cents, the deferred price by only one-half cent. Private telegrams were down by sixteen and eleven-sixteenths cents, so the market sentiment was down. Then, Yuan Heng and Tong Taichang bought in, and the price rose to 703 taels. Suddenly, it fell by seven taels as Da Decheng, Zhi Fengyong, and other firms sold out, reaching 695 taels and five cents. In an instant, it rebounded by ten taels because Fu Yu, Shunli, Yuan Maoyong, Wanxing, and others competed to buy. The settlement price was announced at 706 taels, and the listed price had shrunk by 125 US dollars. Social News

Marshal Foch's Diary of the European War (Continued)

— Translated by Gu Angruo

The two nights of the second and third were relatively silent. On the third, the German army felt weak and began to bombard Ypres in an orderly manner. This was their habit in this situation. At other times, they could only carry out local attacks and had no effect. The war situation on the fourth was also the same.

Now it can be said that their combined attack on Ypres has failed. Although their army and ammunition far exceeded the Allied forces, their struggle against the stone wall of the Allied forces has collapsed. They cannot continue to fight. The German General Staff had to shrink its ambitions.

The enemy felt that it could not overthrow the Allied forces' defense with a full-line general offensive, nor could it occupy the important center of Ypres to directly attack the coast. Therefore, it now wants to change its attack to the two pivots of the convex angle of our defense line, one to the north of Ypres and one to the south of Ypres.

Although the strategic victory that the enemy wanted to achieve was not successful, it could at least consolidate its western front in Flanders with a tactical victory and turn to attack Russia.

It can achieve this goal without occupying Ypres, because attacking both ends of the convex angle can allow it to move artillery closer to the north and south sides, hindering our traffic centered on Ypres and forcing our troops to withdraw from the semi-circular front line.

In this way, after the fierce battle in the east of the city, the two armies will fight again on its north and south sides.

Starting from the fifth, people gained the reinforcement of a new division and launched a large-scale attack to the south of Wesque when we were advancing towards Messines. In the north, the enemy's third reserve army successfully launched a war against Bisquique and Langemark. The remaining enemy troops were not active.

The Battle of Ypres ended on the 13th. The German army attacked the north and south pivots to subdue the convex angle, leading to two major battles that lasted for several days without a victory.

On November 18, the two armies returned to their original defense and the front line was completely stable.

After the war, we immediately took the opportunity to reorganize the army. The commander-in-chief transferred a large number of reinforcements, making it easier for us to start.

Most of our soldiers have been trapped in a dilemma, and their replacement is imminent. I am now beginning to negotiate with the Flanders commander-in-chief on the division of the front line and the deployment of the Allied forces. After several days of deliberation, we reached an agreement on the areas for which each army is responsible for defending.

Because we still cannot be sure of the enemy's situation, we therefore often use aircraft and cavalry to scout whether the enemy has a retreat. We also asked the Dunkirk naval authorities to scout the location of the German army's coastal batteries to the north of Nieuport. After several scouts, we learned that the enemy's trenches were very solid and encountered rifle and artillery fire everywhere. The naval reconnaissance did not dare to venture into the submarine mine area.

The German army is generally holding its ground, impregnable.

The Allied forces have been fighting in Flanders for a long time, the war zone is wide, the participating army elements are complex, and the number of people is not very large. They often arrive slowly and are easily mixed up. Under such complicated circumstances, without unified command, and conducting mixed battles based on the outline and observing the situation clearly, victory is impossible to grasp. There is also one thing whose功不可磨灭 is the most effective contact between the Allied forces and the commanders of each army. This is just another manifestation of the spirit of cooperation of the Allied forces.

The Allied commanders can often meet each other during the day. Every night I ask General Dubail to come to Wanmat to discuss our military affairs and prepare the orders for the next day. His headquarters are located in Lusseburg. At about 10 o'clock, Sir Henry Wilson often brings the war report from the headquarters of the St. Amiens English Army to Cassel, my headquarters, and reports the plans of Commander-in-Chief Flandre for the next day. We are also closely connected with the headquarters of the Belgian Army in Fournes.

The motto of our British Allied forces to be united to have strength has never been more completely implemented than this time. This is the secret of using the weak to defeat the strong and holding on for a full month to achieve victory.

I naturally often have close contact with my commander-in-chief. Although I have not seen him since November 2, we exchange opinions every day. Although he has always recognized the importance of the Flanders war, he could not immediately send sufficient troops. His army has been exhausted after two months of fierce fighting. They also lack ammunition, and he has to consolidate the weak front line. The front line is expanding very quickly, and now the front line from Vosges to the Lys River is 375 miles long.

The scope of the front line is so wide that the two armies are in close contact everywhere, and there is a possibility of bombardment everywhere. These facts are the reason why the reinforcements continue to arrive to participate in the Ypres War. They are also the reason why the participating armies have to fight for a long time, only because there are no other armies to replace them. But they were still able to persevere in the entire evil war, which is really commendable. Now two examples can prove it.

The British First Army has suffered heavy losses since October 31. On that day, it had already begun to retreat, but it stopped and fought back, and its courage was a hundred times greater. The enemy attacked repeatedly and failed. In the end, the enemy was indeed contained and then left the battlefield on November 18.
